 ³  Dear Reader :                                                             ³
 ³                                                                            ³
 ³      As always, we value your opinion.  Improvements are constantly being  ³
 ³  made as a direct result of user input.  If you would like to participate  ³
 ³  in the further enhancement of RCN, or would like to send a letter to the  ³
 ³  editors (or to a writer in particular) please send e-mail to              ³
 ³  an385786@anon.penet.fi.  Note that we are no longer accepting             ³
 ³  subscribers to the magazine.  The reason is that the anon.penet.fi        ³
 ³  server will not let us send attached files over 100k in size unless we    ³
 ³  split them up, and that would be confusing for both us and the readers.   ³
 ³  To make up for that, we offer a WWW site accessible via the Internet.     ³
 ³  All issues will be promptly posted there.  For more information, read     ³
 ³  on.                                                                       ³
 ³                                                                            ³
 ³      In an effort to better interact with our readers, the editors of      ³
 ³  RCN have devised a reader survey, and would appreciate it if you would    ³
 ³  take the time to respond to it.  After completion of the survey, you      ³
 ³  simply need to send it attached to the above e-mail address.  Note that   ³
 ³  we prefer NOT getting messages encoded in MIME format.  We also have a    ³
 ³  voting booth so the readers can give input on their favorite groups.      ³
 ³                                                                            ³
 ³      New this issue are some little twirks that might sizzle your buns!    ³
 ³  For those of you that feel more in control when you can change the        ³
 ³  brightness of the colors on your screen, we now have brightness           ³
 ³  support that can be found in the options menu!                            ³
 ³                                                                            ³
 ³      Don't forget to keep sending in your votes for the groups you feel    ³
 ³  are #1, and test your wits of the scene in our Warez-IQ questionnaire,    ³
 ³  10 new questions in this issue!                                           ³
 ³                                                                            ³
 ³      RCN issues have now been made available to a wider audience thanks    ³
 ³  to our new WebSite courtesy of RATM.  Please feel free to browse around   ³
 ³  - http://www.shu.edu/~importmi/rcn/.  RCN ardently feels that our         ³
 ³  WebSite will satisfy our readers and is a welcome addition to our         ³
 ³  methods of distribution.                                                  ³

 ÉÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍ»
 º                                                                            º
 º  Dear RCN,                                                                 º
 º                                                                            º
 º      First, let me begin by explaining who I am.  I'm Shadow Master,       º
 º  currently supplying for Prestige, formerly having done the same for       º
 º  Legend, Genesis, TDU-JAM!, and Razor 1911.  I've been involved with the   º
 º  scene and all its politics and such for 6 years, so I trust you'll all    º
 º  understand that I know what I'm talking about when it comes to the        º
 º  scene.  In all of my 6 years, I have never seen a more disgraceful,       º
 º  uninformed, and downright idiotic assessment as Instant Rage's            º
 º  commentary on Napalm.                                                     º
 º                                                                            º
 º      Instant Rage claims that Napalm has "speed" and it's this speed       º
 º  which allows them to be so fast that they beat veteran groups.  Let me    º
 º  clue everyone in.  Napalm's "speed," as evidenced by the incredible       º
 º  number of problems found with every game, derives from the fact that      º
 º  they blatantly ignore the established rules of fair play.  EVERY other    º
 º  group, upon getting a release, takes the time and effort necessary to     º
 º  release a working product, while Napalm has chosen to bastardize the      º
 º  system.                                                                   º
 º                                                                            º
 º      Instant Rage claims that such idiocy is "perfecting the art of        º
 º  releasing."  The established rules of the scene DEMAND that a release be  º
 º  working before it is given to the general public.  Napalm has chosen to   º
 º  ignore the rules as fairly established by the games groups in good        º
 º  faith, simply because they would otherwise be slaughtered when it came    º
 º  time for competition.                                                     º
 º                                                                            º
 º      Let me give you a metaphor to consider what Napalm is doing.  Let's   º
 º  say you want to purchase a TV.  Which one would you be happier with, one  º
 º  that you got that worked straight out of the box, or the one that was     º
 º  broken, forcing you to call the mechanic to repair it.  Obviously you'd   º
 º  want the first one, which is why games groups decided that a  release     º
 º  must be working when put out.  One would think this is common sense.      º
 º  Napalm's feeble efforts were mistakes, plain and simple, not some grand   º
 º  new way of releasing.                                                     º
 º                                                                            º
 º      In the old days, when a release did not work, another group would     º
 º  re-release it and slam on the group who put out the non working version   º
 º  because the 1st group made a mistake.  The only reason other groups       º
 º  haven't been doing that lately is that they made the mistake of trusting  º
 º  Napalm to play fair, and not release the games until they were 100%       º
 º  working.  The other groups assumed that Napalm was following the rules    º
 º  of fair play, just as they were, and ceased trying to release their       º
 º  version when the Napalm version was released.  I will swear right now     º
 º  that if Napalm does this again, even if the game is 40 Disks, I will      º
 º  re-release every single disk and have their release nuked off every       º
 º  major board and Internet site, and I promise that it will happen,         º
 º  because people know and respect the rules which Napalm has so blatantly   º
 º  chosen to ignore.                                                         º
 º                                                                            º
 º      Don't get me wrong, if Napalm has a game far in advance of others     º
 º  and puts it out, but it needs a fix, I won't release it all again.        º
 º  Napalm has chosen to use this non-working strategy as a cheap way of      º
 º  winning races with other groups when they know they are in danger of      º
 º  being beaten.  So if a game's in the possession of several groups and     º
 º  Napalm tries their dirty tricks again, I will be on their ass before      º
 º  they can blink, seeing to it that they get what they deserve, which is    º
 º  nothing more than the contempt of all respectable groups and the loss of  º
 º  credits on boards and sites worldwide.                                    º
 º                                                                            º
 º      In conclusion, while Napalm may be trying to prove themselves, the    º
 º  only thing they have proven is that they cannot win fairly and must       º
 º  resort to using deceit to even attempt to compete with others.  If        º
 º  Napalm wishes to regain any respectability, they must play by the rules   º
 º  and beat the groups at their own game, as has been the custom for as      º
 º  long as the scene has been established.  It's better to have not          º
 º  released a game then to resort to trickery and attempt to pass it off as  º
 º  victory.  Others may have chosen to write off Napalm's foolishness in     º
 º  the past, but things will change.  To be the man, you've got to BEAT the  º
 º  man.  Word up to  Napalm, the Master's watching, so you had better get    º
 º  with the program, and get with it fast.                                   º
 º                                                                            º
 º                                               Signed,                      º
 º                                                  Shadow Master             º
 º                                                                            º

 ÉÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍ»
 º                                                                            º
 º    Reporter : Rebel Chicken             Interviewee : Prophet              º
 º    Subject  : Napalm vs. Prestige       Affiliation : NPM Leader           º
 º                                                                            º
 ÈÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍ¼
 ÉÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍ»
 º                                                                            º
 º  RCN : NPM (Napalm) was originally a SNES consoles group, but has in the   º
 º        past few months switched to doing PC games, what caused this        º
 º        switch from SNES to PC?                                             º
 º                                                                            º
 º  NPM : NPM was first started in the SNES consoles scene by Daviolator,     º
 º        but then the SNES consoles scene died because Sony Playstation and  º
 º        Sega Saturn took over.  Daviolator came to me and asked me to       º
 º        start NPM PC.  It was started only for fun, we here at NPM don't    º
 º        care about what people have to say about us.  We just do it for     º
 º        fun.  We like to keep a nice relationship with everyone in the      º
 º        scene if possible.  After Daviolator called me to start NPM PC, I   º
 º        contacted Hannibal to start up NPM, but he was also contacted by    º
 º        Cyber Angel to start up TRN (Tyranny), but somehow, I caught        º
 º        Hannibal's attention and he joined NPM instead.  From there we      º
 º        began NPM. At first, I recruited many RiSC couriers because I have  º
 º        been in RiSC for a long time and I know many traders very well.     º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RCN : NPM has done extremely well in releasing games, and it beats many   º
 º        other games groups such as RZR (Razor 1911) and HBD (Hybrid).  But  º
 º        many people say that nearly all of NPM releases do *NOT* working,   º
 º        and according to a RZR member, RZR has decided that they will       º
 º        release a game even if NPM has already released it because RZR      º
 º        assumes that anything from NPM will not work.                       º
 º                                                                            º
 º  NPM : Well it is true we had a few releases that did not work, but we     º
 º        always fix our releases unlike RZR.  When they fuck up, they leave  º
 º        it that way and tend to ignore their faults.  I admit we have had   º
 º        many careless mistakes in our releases but this is only because we  º
 º        are a new group.  We learn from our mistakes and as you can see     º
 º        currently we are doing great with our releases and there are no     º
 º        more fuck ups.                                                      º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RCN : Yes, that is true, NPM has not released any nonworking releases in  º
 º        the past 2 weeks, but it also has not released period.  Why is      º
 º        that so?  Is NPM merely in a slump, or is there something more      º
 º        going on in there effecting the future of the group?                º
 º                                                                            º
 º  NPM : That is again true, we are in a slump.  I can say we have lost      º
 º        many releases to PSG (Prestige), they seem to be a great group      º
 º        with a lot of talent and a nice future ahead of them.  As always,   º
 º        in NPM we only do this for fun, we don't worry much about who's     º
 º        better and who's not.  We tend to not care what others think about  º
 º        us.  We only do this for our own pleasure and we try as much        º
 º        possible to support the scene.  We are currently we making some     º
 º        changes in the group to help NPM's future making it stable and      º
 º        alive for many years.                                               º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RCN : What are some of these changes being planned?  Perhaps NPM needs a  º
 º        new council of leaders, or a fresh crew of suppliers?               º
 º                                                                            º
 º  NPM : Well, this is for me to know and for people to find out!  Like I    º
 º        said, we like to keep this group up and running for many years but  º
 º        I know that people tend to leave the scene for many reasons.  I     º
 º        try make sure that there's always a replacement for positions in    º
 º        case someone leaves for the scene.  NPM is a very young group, and  º
 º        many people in NPM are currently still going to college and are in  º
 º        their 20's although there are a few of us who are over the hill.    º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RCN : Would you consider the competition between PSG and NPM to be        º
 º        completely friendly?  For example, PSG has a quote that says "If    º
 º        you guys nuke our PSG Euro Edition, you guys should nuke NPM's      º
 º        Tony Larusa 96 Edition".                                            º
 º                                                                            º
 º  NPM : This is what I really hate about the scene, one reason I tend to    º
 º        just like to stay low profile and courier!  In the scene, there is  º
 º        no friendly competition.  I can say for a fact that PSG is giving   º
 º        us a hard time to release, there's no need to hide the truth.       º
 º        Yes, I've noticed PSG's quote too and I don't like it one bit but   º
 º        what can I do?  The whole scene tends to hate NPM for some reason.  º
 º        They always have some bad reasons to blame things on us but we      º
 º        don't bother to fight it because we simply don't care!              º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RCN : Both NPM and PSG released "Battle Arena : Toshinden".  However,     º
 º        the cracks for both games are also identical, and there are         º
 º        accusations from PSG that NPM *STOLE* the PSG crack, is that true?  º
 º                                                                            º
 º  NPM : Well, ever since NPM started releasing, there were always so many   º
 º        people ragging on us from other groups.  They showed no respect to  º
 º        a new group.  This is entirely understandable since I don't give    º
 º        much respect to new groups either.  But groups have constantly put  º
 º        the blame on NPM for everything.  Other groups always blame us for  º
 º        things like stealing, and for things like how much NPM fucked up.   º
 º        We simply don't care, we're here just to have fun.  We don't care   º
 º        if nobody wants to download NPM releases or if nobody wants to      º
 º        join NPM.                                                           º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RCN : You still didn't answer my question about the crack.  According to  º
 º        PSG, the NPM and PSG crack for "Battle Arena : Toshinden" had the   º
 º        exact same exact time stamp, and the NPM cracker that supposedly    º
 º        cracked the game admitted that he didn't make the crack.            º
 º                                                                            º
 º  NPM : Well, Wolverine didn't crack the game but I can say that someone    º
 º        else from NPM did crack the game but his name will not be revealed  º
 º        because he chose not to be mentioned in the scene.  I have no       º
 º        evidence of the fact that we cracked the game.  There is no way I   º
 º        can prove myself to people that we actually cracked the game.       º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RCN : Many of the top games groups ask that their BBS sysops and some of  º
 º        their members to pay the leaders money, so they could go out and    º
 º        *BUY* releases.  Is that the way NPM works?  If so, how much money  º
 º        does NPM spend a month *BUYING* releases, and how much money do     º
 º        they spend paying their suppliers?                                  º
 º                                                                            º
 º  NPM : Yes, NPM has a big monthly budget like many other groups.  We are   º
 º        doing this all out of our own pockets because again we are here     º
 º        just to have fun.  I can't really say how much money we use         º
 º        monthly but we are paying for every one of those releases.  We      º
 º        never ask other people to pay us money, that is lame I think.  The  º
 º        scene is not to make money but to have fun!  Well, we can't         º
 º        explain the process of getting a release faster than other groups   º
 º        since all the groups get the games at the same time!  Speed is      º
 º        based on who works the fastest and who is able to get the game      º
 º        cracked first, and test the release, then release it!  Everyone     º
 º        was saying that NPM's main supplier was Fan Fan La Tulipe           º
 º        (ex-TDU-JAM! Leader), but that is total bullshit because we don't   º
 º        even know each other.                                               º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RCN : There are rumors that Daviolator works for Acclaim, and that is     º
 º        why you guys release a lot of Acclaim titles, is that true?         º
 º                                                                            º
 º  NPM : Daviolator doesn't work for Acclaim, but he knows a guy in Acclaim  º
 º        that gives us the games even before it hits mass production.        º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RCN : What was the best game NPM ever released?                           º
 º                                                                            º
 º  NPM : Well, I think our best release was "Descent 2" even though we       º
 º        fucked up on it!  The thing is, many people think NPM put out 10    º
 º        fixes but the thing is, we only put out 1 fix that fixed the sound  º
 º        problem and the level 3 CD-ROM check.  People must understand that  º
 º        we couldn't test out the whole game and play test it for every      º
 º        level.  We only got so far as level 2.                              º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RCN : In your opinion, how would you rank the top games groups?           º
 º                                                                            º
 º  NPM : If you want the truth, nothing but the truth, then I must say that  º
 º        PSG is #1, NPM is #2, HBD is #3, and RZR is #4, but keep in mind    º
 º        EVERYTHING changes, it's the law of nature!  I think that there     º
 º        are no real friends in the games scene even though I would really   º
 º        want to have some friends with the groups out there.  We would      º
 º        rather make friends and not enemies, but then again, it's hard to   º
 º        trust someone in the scene.  I think the groups out there RAG on    º
 º        NPM so much because they fear NPM.  At this moment it seems to me   º
 º        that RZR has died off, and the only groups out there are HBD, PSG,  º
 º        and NPM!  I repeat, RZR has died off!!                              º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RCN : What about the games group DNX (Dynamix) that released "Duke Nukem  º
 º        3D" and the games group ROR (Release on Rampage) that released      º
 º        argh.. a nonworking version of "Cyberia 2" and a lame "WarCraft     º
 º        2/Command and Conquer toolkit"?                                     º
 º                                                                            º
 º  NPM : Well DNX is practically dead since all the memebers of DNX have     º
 º        left to join PSG.  ROR was never really in the picture.  It seems   º
 º        to me they put out all the beta releases of games.                  º
 º                                                                            º

 ÉÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍ»
 º                                                                            º
 º    Reporter : Rebel Chicken             Interviewee : Shadow Master        º
 º    Subject  : Prestige vs. Napalm       Affiliation : PSG Leader           º
 º                                                                            º
 ÈÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍ¼
 ÉÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍ»
 º                                                                            º
 º  RCN : PSG (Prestige) has done extremely well recently, and some           º
 º        attribute it's success to the fact that nearly all of DNX           º
 º        (Dynamix) supplier's have left DNX and joined PSG, is that          º
 º        statement valid?                                                    º
 º                                                                            º
 º  PSG : PSG would be doing just fine on its own.  However, the DNX guys     º
 º        have provided plenty of support.  While not wholy responsible for   º
 º        the success, they are a great contributing factor.                  º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RCN : There's a quote by PSG that says "If you guys nuke our PSG Euro     º
 º        Edition, you guys should nuke Napalm's Tony Larusa 1996 Edition",   º
 º        to what does that refer to, and why was that quote directed at NPM  º
 º        (Napalm)?                                                           º
 º                                                                            º
 º  PSG : I wrote that quote for people new to warez.  That was directed at   º
 º        NPM because two of their traders, mainly Darkside and Shatter       º
 º        Star, began nuking PSG's version of Sensible Soccer on FTP sites    º
 º        saying it was a dupe of an earlier release from December.  This     º
 º        was a brand new edition, sold separately, exactly like "Tony        º
 º        Larussa 3 1996 Edition".  A version had come out before, but NPM    º
 º        released the 1996 Edition which was sold separately and a brand     º
 º        new release.  I was just pointing out that by their logic, "Tony    º
 º        Larussa 3 1996 Edition" would deserve to be nuked as well.          º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RCN : There has also been a little upheaval about the release "Battle     º
 º        Arena : Toshinden", what was that all about?                        º
 º                                                                            º
 º  PSG : PSG released "Battle Arena : Toshinden" and uploaded around 3       º
 º        disks of the game on a RiSC FTP site called LA.  I then had to      º
 º        reboot my computer and when I finally got back on and resumed my    º
 º        upload only to see that there was a NPM version already on LA.      º
 º        After winning a spreading war with NPM, The Speed Racer from RZR    º
 º        (Razor 1911) called me and asked me why the NPM crack for "Battle   º
 º        Arena : Toshinden" was the same as PSG's crack.  The crack in the   º
 º        NPM and PSG releases were both named the same TSDCRK.ZIP and when   º
 º        the cracked EXEs from both version were examined, they were found   º
 º        to be the exact same, down to the time and date stamps.  We also    º
 º        found out that the first person to leech the 3 disks off of LA was  º
 º        Prophet, leader of NPM.  Grudge did not expect there to be a NPM    º
 º        version of "Battle Arena : Toshinden" since he already saw the PSG  º
 º        version on LA, and was shocked to see a NPM version on LA minutes   º
 º        later.  Grudge informed me that that Wolverine, the cracker listed  º
 º        in the NPM .NFO, would have had to have crack the game in about 1   º
 º        minute.  The evidence was pretty clear as to what NPM did, and PSG  º
 º        was far from pleased.                                               º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RCN : It is pretty clear then that NPM must have stole the crack from     º
 º        PSG.  However, according to Prophet, he told me that he didn't do   º
 º        it, and that a special anonymous cracker cracked the release, do    º
 º        you believe Prophet?                                                º
 º                                                                            º
 º  PSG : Why would Prophet admit to stealing a crack, the uproar from the    º
 º        rest of the scene would be incredible.  NPM would lose any respect  º
 º        it had.  I do not believe Prophet at all.  Even his own members     º
 º        speak differently.                                                  º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RCN : So basically, Prophet is trying to pull an O.J. Simpson?            º
 º                                                                            º
 º  PSG : Yes.                                                                º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RCN : Why has so many DNX suppliers flooded to join PSG?  What attracted  º
 º        them over to PSG?                                                   º
 º                                                                            º
 º  PSG : I'm not quite sure what attracted them, so I'll make an attempt to  º
 º        guess.  A merger was proposed at one point in time between DNX and  º
 º        PSG, but it fell apart.  I believe that several DNX members, such   º
 º        as Hemp Hoodlum, The Renegade Chemist, and Zeus became tired of     º
 º        being the only ones to support DNX.  Hemp Hoodlum withdrew the DNX  º
 º        and PSG merger apparently without telling The Renegade Chemist or   º
 º        Zeus.  Several days later, The Renegade Chemist asked if PSG had    º
 º        decided to merge, and when I mentioned that Hemp Hoodlum had        º
 º        withdrawn the proposal, he got extremely pissed.  5 minutes later,  º
 º        The Renegade Chemist, Zeus, and a few others DNX members joined     º
 º        PSG.  About an hour later, it appeared that the rest of DNX didn't  º
 º        think they could handle the group without the members who left, so  º
 º        Hemp Hoodlum and several others joined PSG.                         º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RCN : How would you rate PSG compared to the games group RZR?             º
 º                                                                            º
 º  PSG : In regards to RZR, I believe that PSG is, at least for the moment,  º
 º        in a much better position.  RZR's suppliers curerntly seem to lack  º
 º        motivation, and their crackers never seem to be around.  The RZR    º
 º        staff has assured me that things will change in June.  They have    º
 º        the ability to beat PSG, whether or not they have the desire is     º
 º        another question.                                                   º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RCN : How would you rate PSG compared to the games group HBD (Hybrid)?    º
 º                                                                            º
 º  PSG : HBD, on the other hand, while able to put up an extremely good      º
 º        showing, lacks suppliers from the U.S., because of that, it is not  º
 º        in a position to challenge PSG.  Should they gain suppliers from    º
 º        the U.S., then they would be a force to be reckoned with.           º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RCN : What about other groups such as ROR ( Release on Rampage), who      º
 º        brag about great releases such as "WarCraft 2/Command and Conquer   º
 º        Toolkit" do you think they'll be in competing status with other     º
 º        good games groups?                                                  º
 º                                                                            º
 º  PSG : While I must commend ROR and other groups of that type for their    º
 º        dedication in continuing to provide new warez, they are not in any  º
 º        position to compete with the more established games groups. As far  º
 º        as I can see, they do not possess either the suppliers nor the      º
 º        crackers needed in order to compete with the current top games      º
 º        groups.                                                             º
 º                                                                            º
 º                                                                            º

 ÉÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍ»
 º                                                                            º
 º    Reporter : Rebel Chicken             Interviewee : Shatter              º
 º    Subject  : Shatter Star              Affiliation : DOD/NPM/RiSC         º
 º                                                                            º
 ÈÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍ¼
 ÉÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍ»
 º                                                                            º
 º  RCN : Shatter, we all know that you are an integral part of groups such   º
 º        as DOD (Drink or Die), NPM (Napalm), and RiSC (Rise in Superior     º
 º        Couriering), but what's of most interest to people is your job as   º
 º        a RiSC member, what do you do for that group?                       º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RSC : Well, being a member of RiSC would probably have to be the hardest  º
 º        of my jobs, because it's a full-time job, unlike being in a         º
 º        releasing group, when you're in a big-time couriering group like    º
 º        RiSC, you have to spend a lot more time on it, and I have that      º
 º        time because I don't have a job and I go to school.  But my main    º
 º        role in the group is supposed to be a "coordinator" which           º
 º        basically means that I manage one of our FTP sites and make sure    º
 º        all the traders are active on there and the traders that need       º
 º        accounts on those FTP sites get them.  What interests me and keeps  º
 º        me a RiSC member is that it's all so fun.  I really enjoy working   º
 º        with the members of RiSC.                                           º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RCN : Which FTP site do you manage "coordinate"?                          º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RSC : I manage and coordinate one of our FTP sites called "LA", most      º
 º        people that are on it are familiar with its affiliations.  There    º
 º        are also other methods of coordinating which I think I should keep  º
 º        to myself.                                                          º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RCN : OH, so you threaten people with a GUN hey?  Anyways, you mentioned  º
 º        that you make sure that all the traders are active, what happens    º
 º        when a trader is not active?                                        º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RSC : When a trader is not active, I send them a little email asking      º
 º        them why they haven't been active on that site.  BBS couriers are   º
 º        given a little more slack, but if they are a regular Internet FTP   º
 º        trader is expected to do 100-300 megs a week there, and for 2       º
 º        weeks they don't even trade, you have to wonder why.  And if I      º
 º        don't get a reply back, well, that hasn't happened yet and I'm not  º
 º        exaclty sure what I would do at that point.  I would probably try   º
 º        to contact him on the phone.                                        º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RCN : OKay, so they usually don't just get kicked out of the group?       º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RSC : RiSC isn't that strict, no usually not, but obviously if they say   º
 º        "No, I don't want to courier anymore because you guys suck" or if   º
 º        they refuse to do anything, then yeah, we kick them out.  But if    º
 º        they have a valid reason for not couriering as much, it's           º
 º        perfectly understandable.                                           º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RCN : I remember that NOT too long ago, Mikeysoft was one of the 3 RiSC   º
 º        leaders, now there's only 2.  What happened to him? Did he refuse   º
 º        to work? Did he say "you guys suck"?                                º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RSC : Ahh yes, Mikeysoft, I really didn't know him that good, nor did I   º
 º        talk to him a lot, and I probably know as much as the common        º
 º        person out there.  I don't think I got into RiSC until a little     º
 º        after he was kicked out.  As far as I know, he didn't do anything   º
 º        wrong, and I know he ran a board called Final Frontier.  I don't    º
 º        hink he refused to work, or he told us we suck, I guess we kicked   º
 º        him out for the saftey of the group and because he was just         º
 º        sitting there.                                                      º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RCN : So Mikeysoft never did anything for the group RiSC?  He was just    º
 º        sitting there?  Did he go raving mad when he found out he got       º
 º        kicked out of RiSC even thought it was for RiSC's safety?           º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RSC : As far as I know, no.  Of course, I haven't been in the scene a     º
 º        long time to know the whole story.  I don't think he reacted at     º
 º        all.  No one really said anything after that about him being        º
 º        kicked out.  And I think he knows why he was kicked out.            º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RCN : How would you rate RiSC compared to the other courier groups out    º
 º        there, for example, against fATE (Fast Action Trade Exchange),      º
 º        fATE has an awesome system of IRC couriering, but anybody who's     º
 º        anybody knows that they're lacking in sites, and anybody who's      º
 º        anybody knows RiSC does not have a #RiSCfiles, but that RiSC has    º
 º        the best BBSes and FTP sites in the world, and can courier.         º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RSC : RiSC has been around the longest in the scene, RTS (Request to      º
 º        Send) has been around quite awhile but I don't it's older than      º
 º        RiSC.  I must admit that fATE spreads pirated software to more      º
 º        people and more feds out there, but RiSC definitely has the         º
 º        fastest warez on the FTP sites.  Since most of the uploading        º
 º        occurs at the top FTP sites, groups with slower FTP sites get it a  º
 º        bit slower.  Now, I'm not saying fATE get's warez 10 hours later,   º
 º        but with today's speed and couriers, it's all a matter of minutes.  º
 º        And that is what counts on the FTP sites.                           º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RCN : How important do you think it is for a courier group to have an     º
 º        offering channel?                                                   º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RSC : RiSC doesn't have an offering channel, and I don't think we will    º
 º        EVER have one.  I support the idea of getting the warez out to      º
 º        everyone, but personally I think fATE has assumed that role.  RiSC  º
 º        doesn't distribute files on IRC channels simply because we do not   º
 º        want 100 people in the group, just offering all day.  We like to    º
 º        have our group small, and as best as it can be.                     º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RCN : So you're saying that fATE is slow, or at least slower than RiSC?   º
 º        Really?  That can't be..                                            º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RSC : I really think the majority of the files are spread on the top FTP  º
 º        sites.  Like I said, it's all a matter of minutes.  If I put up a   º
 º        10 disk release on a RiSC site.  Someone will at the same time      º
 º        leech it at say 100kb.  They will have it on their shell in about   º
 º        2 minutes.  Then he uploads it to another site which takes a        º
 º        couple minutes, and then it's on the fATE sites.  You don't see a   º
 º        lot of files coming from the less active sites do you??             º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RCN : I don't like getting on slow sites.  Since the gap between being    º
 º        fast and slow is only a matter of minutes, how do you get it on     º
 º        the RiSC FTP sites so fast?  You are considered one of the fastest  º
 º        FTP traders around.                                                 º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RSC : Well I think I am fortunate to be on these FTP sites and to be in   º
 º        RiSC of course.  I think people consider me one of the best         º
 º        because I was taught by the best, Darkhosis.  The competition is    º
 º        so hard these days, if you go out of your computer room to take a   º
 º        piss, you might come back and see a 40 disk release on a site that  º
 º        you wanted to trade on.                                             º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RCN : I take it you don't piss much then, or you must have a bottle in    º
 º        front of you right now.  On the note of NPM, they haven't released  º
 º        in about 2 weeks now, are there problems fostering in NPM?          º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RSC : Haha, no, but my bathroom is close to this room though.  Napalm     º
 º        hasn't been releasing much because we are "testing" our members     º
 º        loyalty in a way, to see who ditches the group when we are in a     º
 º        slump.  I must admit PSG (Prestige) is kicking our NPM in the ass   º
 º        right now with their releases, but I assure you NPM will be back.   º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RCN : Is there a chance that RiSC will ever TEST it's members loyalty by  º
 º        not coureiring for a week and a half?                               º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RSC : If you look at that, it is kind of hard, I mean RiSC isn't going    º
 º        to stop anyone from releasing, and the couriers DON'T want to stop  º
 º        trading, believe me.                                                º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RCN : Ah, now, on the note of DOD, many ppl know that DOD is definitely   º
 º        not doing as well as they used to, Quackers, an ex-DOD council,     º
 º        and 3 of DOD's best suppliers recently left DOD to join PWA.        º
 º        Rumors are that Jimmy Jamez hardly has control of the group         º
 º        anymore, and that DOD is basically going downhill and it's a        º
 º        matter of time before it dies, is that true?                        º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RSC : Tough question, I'm afraid to answer that because I have been in    º
 º        DOD for maybe a week at the most.  But I have been hanging out in   º
 º        #DOD since I have been in the scene and I am good friends with      º
 º        Lester and Hellraiser, and the other DOD seniors.  But this all     º
 º        happened before I joined so no one told me because it was to kept   º
 º        between DOD seniors.  I really don't think DOD will die just        º
 º        because of it gets so much respect from the scene and because       º
 º        there are great people in the group.  Every group goes through      º
 º        slumps, and it seems that all the releasing groups I am in right    º
 º        now are in slumps.                                                  º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RCN : May be you bring bad luck?                                          º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RSC : I think I bring good luck since I am very fortunate to be in the    º
 º        groups I am in.                                                     º
 º                                                                            º
 º                                                                            º

 ÈÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍ¼
 ÉÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍ»
 º                                                                            º
 º  RCN : You are currently one of the leaders of the outstanding courier     º
 º        group DGT (Digital Traders), how did you become a leader of DGT?    º
 º        Were you one of the original founders?                              º
 º                                                                            º
 º  DGT : Yes, I'm currently a leader and a founder of DGT along with Silent  º
 º        Mobius and Devast.                                                  º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RCN : What were your affiliations before you were a DGT leader?           º
 º                                                                            º
 º  DGT : I was the vice-president of MC (MindCrash).  After the downfall of  º
 º        MC, I formed a group called IMP (Impulse) of which I was president  º
 º        of.                                                                 º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RCN : How did the downfall of MC occur?  Some accuse you of being the     º
 º        trigger of MC's downfall earlier this year, and that you            º
 º        essentially killed MC so you could form IMP?                        º
 º                                                                            º
 º  DGT : The downfall of MC was imminent, but I was not at fault.  The       º
 º        Wicked One, who was the President of MC, and whom I have the        º
 º        deepest respect for, left MC all at a really bad time.  I admit     º
 º        that I made some mistakes but they were in no way the cause of the  º
 º        downfall of MC.  I didn't kill or have anything to do with killing  º
 º        MC for the sole purpose of being able to create IMP.  The creation  º
 º        of IMP came about after the eventual death of MC.                   º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RCN : The Wicked One said that you already had IMP in mind even before    º
 º        you left MC, is that true?                                          º
 º                                                                            º
 º  DGT : Yes and no.  After The Wicked One "left", Avoozl came and took his  º
 º        place as the leader of MC which caused a lot of problems.  It was   º
 º        then that the IDEA was brought to my attention that I should start  º
 º        my own courier group.  I didn't come up with the idea, I only       º
 º        pursued it after MC was actually dead.                              º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RCN : Who brought you this IDEA?                                          º
 º                                                                            º
 º  DGT : Headbanger (MC Council) and Sinning Soul both felt it best to       º
 º        leave the group.   Since I was a dedicated member, I asked them     º
 º        not to, and I tried to keep MC alive.  However, my attempts were    º
 º        futile and MC was quickly withering away.  I tried my best, but I   º
 º        felt that it was time to bail out. I contacted Headbanger and       º
 º        Sinning Soul voice on a telephone conference, and we decided to     º
 º        create IMP.                                                         º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RCN : How did IMP die? I ask that since I sure don't see it around        º
 º        anyomre, did it perhaps merge into another courier group?           º
 º                                                                            º
 º  DGT : Yes, IMP had surpassed my expectations in every possible way.  We   º
 º        had over 50 members within one week, and had to support major       º
 º        release groups such as ROR and Skull Control.  However, the         º
 º        success of IMP was a bit too much for me to handle.  I didn't have  º
 º        the time to do all the work, so I decided to enter a 3 way merge    º
 º        between DGT, tNt Traders, and one other courier group.  I           º
 º        contacted Silent Mobius and Devast to find out more about the       º
 º        merge, but I then found out that the information concerning the     º
 º        merge was completely incorrect.  Then, out of the blue clear sky,   º
 º        came talks of another merger which I pursued.  After numerous days  º
 º        of negotiations, this other merger between IMP and DGT took place.  º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RCN : There are some rumors that the only reason DGT wanted a merger      º
 º        with IMP was because of Swamper.  DGT felt that Swamper was the     º
 º        only courier from IMP that they felt were up to standards with      º
 º        DGT, and that they highly sought after him.  Is that true?          º
 º                                                                            º
 º  DGT : NO!  That is not true at all.  They didn't even know Swamper's      º
 º        kick ass courier ability until after the merge had already taken    º
 º        place.  I have worked with Devast and Silent Mobius in MC before    º
 º        and I knew that they are good leaders and that they are people I    º
 º        could count if I were to be absent from the group.  I can count on  º
 º        them to make sure that everything is kept under control             º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RCN : Devast, also a leader of DGT, was once kicked out of MC, do you     º
 º        feel that his expulsion from MC effected the way you two work       º
 º        together or on how you two view DMT (DarkMoon traders), the new     º
 º        courier group that is run by The Wicked One, ex-MC President?       º
 º        (RCN #15 - Bob)                                                     º
 º                                                                            º
 º  DGT : No, Devast was kicked out of MC shortly after I joined up with MC.  º
 º        I don't have any animosity towards DMT or The Wicked One.  He has   º
 º        earned my respect and he is still a good friend.  I wish DMT the    º
 º        best of luck and if they ever want to have a courier competition,   º
 º        DGT is up to the challenge!                                         º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RCN : How has the competition and eventual loss of the DGT vs. AMN        º
 º        (Amnesia) courier competition effected DGT as a whole?              º
 º        (RCN #14, #15 - Bob)                                                º
 º                                                                            º
 º  DGT : Honestly, it did us a world of good.  We showed the world that we   º
 º        could hold our own with some of the best, and that gave us all      º
 º        great desire to continue to excel.  Besides, we only lost by 27     º
 º        megs, which if given 1 more hour, we could have easily beat AMN.    º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RCN : Many consider that DGT, at it's current level, has more than        º
 º        surpassed MC's courier ability even at it's peak.  How has your     º
 º        experience as vice-president of MC prepared you for being a leader  º
 º        in DGT?                                                             º
 º                                                                            º
 º  DGT : I say that without MC, I wouldn't be where I am today.  I have      º
 º        learned so much from being a leader of MC since I made my mistakes  º
 º        with MC and have learned from them and in turn, I know what not to  º
 º        do with DGT.                                                        º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RCN : What were these mistakes which you made?                            º
 º                                                                            º
 º  DGT : Well, I know about EGO now.  I was on my high horse and ordered     º
 º        people around trying to get everything organized.  I have refined   º
 º        my organizational skills intto an art form.                         º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RCN : Even though DGT only lost to AMN by a mere 27 megs in that one      º
 º        week contest, do you consider DGT as a whole, a match for AMN?      º
 º                                                                            º
 º  DGT : Yes, I consider us a match for all the courier groups out there,    º
 º        and if given 1 more hour, DGT would have won.  DGT led the contest  º
 º        most of the time, and given the proper incentives we can do         º
 º        wonders!                                                            º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RCN : All groups?  Do you feel that DGT is a match for groups such as     º
 º        RiSC and EVR (EVERLAST)?                                            º
 º                                                                            º
 º  DGT : Yes and no.  Again, under the proper conditions, we can hold our    º
 º        own, taking nothing away from RiSC or EVR, but if we can compete    º
 º        with AMN, I feel we can compete with anybody.                       º
 º                                                                            º
 º  RCN : When you say that you're a match for all the courier groups out     º
 º        there, how can you assume so?  DGT lost to AMN by a mere 27 megs,   º

 º  RCN : First off, rumors have it that RAP (Rapier) started as a result of  º

 º        know many people in MAL in the end, since a lot of the old guys     º

 º        using extrapolated credit cards on long distance phone calls.       º

 ÉÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍ»
 º                                                                            º
 º    Author  : g0d                                                           º
 º    Subject : Zieg Passes Away                                              º
 º                                                                            º
 ÈÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍ¼
 ÉÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍ»
 º                                                                            º
 º      This letter is my way of paying respect to Markus Zoepel, also known  º
 º  as "Zieg".  Many of you out there in the scene were probably good         º
 º  friends with Zieg.  He was a great guy who gave more than he expected to  º
 º  receive.  He was a long time member of the scene and loved his days with  º
 º  the couriering group fATE, Fast Action Trade Exchange.  I ask that he     º
 º  not be forgotten as so many people who come and go in the scene are.      º
 º  Markus deserves to be remembered for his many great achievements both on  º
 º  the Internet and off.  In life, he leaves behind a loving wife and two    º
 º  beautiful children ages 10 and 2.                                         º
 º                                                                            º
 º      Markus was system administrator and part owner of ISYS Technologies   º
 º  an ISP (Internet Service Provider) located in Canada.  He had taken this  º
 º  ISP from a mere 8 node system to the becoming the largest ISP in Ontario  º
 º  over a period of 8 short months.  He was simply a genius with the         º
 º  Internet and was always willing to offer a helping hand to anyone who     º
 º  needed it.                                                                º
 º                                                                            º
 º      Markus was one of few people whom I consider a close friend and I     º
 º  will not allow him to simply be forgotten.  There is a web page going up  º
 º  in his memory at "www.isys.ca" and any email you wish to send to pay      º
 º  your repects may be directed to "staff@isys.ca".  I will personally make  º
 º  sure that this mail reaches his wife, or to whomever it is addressed.     º
 º                                                                            º
 º      Markus would have wanted to tell all of you whom he knew how much he  º
 º  enjoyed hanging out on IRC with you all.  It was really a big part of     º
 º  his life and he loved every minute of it.  I don't think he would have    º
 º  traded one minute of it for anything.  Markus was a true Internet junky   º
 º  as a lot of us are.  Even if you didn't know him, but would like to pay   º
 º  respect to a fellow Internet junky, please do so.  All letters will be    º
 º  set up on a web page which will always stand in memory of Zieg.  In a     º
 º  world so fast paced and unforgiving, let's try to at least give support   º
 º  to those whom he loved and those who loved him back.  It is the least we  º
 º  can do.                                                                   º
 º                                                                            º
 º      Markus died of a brain anurism.  The doctor said that there was       º
 º  nothing that could have been done to either detect or to prevent this     º
 º  from ever happening.  Right up until the moment it happened, Markus was   º
 º  fine.  And then, all of a sudden, out of the blue, with no warning, he    º
 º  simply passed away.  The loss of a friend is always rough, but in this    º
 º  case it is probably the hardest loss I have ever had to deal with.        º
 º  Markus, if you're out there somewhere, take it easy bro, we will meet     º
 º  again.. some day.. and I promise I will bring you that day's new          º
 º  release.  You will be missed old friend.  And in my case, you will never  º
 º  be forgotten.  Save a spot at a half decent terminal up there for me bro  º
 º  :)...                                                                     º
 º                                                                            º
 º      Life is such a fragile thing.  We all take it for granted, but this   º
 º  goes to show you, make every minute count because your next minute, may   º
 º  be your last...                                                           º
 º                                                                            º
 º                                               Sincerely,                   º
 º                                                          g0d               º
 º                                                                            º
 ÇÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄ¶
 º                                                                            º
 º  ZOEPEL, Markus Lefebvre                                                   º
 º                                                                            º
 º      In loving memory of Markus Lefebvre-Zoepel who died Thursday          º
 º  evening, May 30th 1996, at the Sudbury General Hospital at the age of     º
 º  29.  He married Roxann Corston in Sudbury in 1993.  He was dedicated,     º
 º  noble and extremely loyal to his family, friends and business.  He knew   º
 º  his calling in life and was a genius at it.  He thoroughly enjoyed        º
 º  fishing, motor biking, canoeing, all outdoor activities, and especially   º
 º  computers and the Internet.  His children and family were his life.       º
 º                                                                            º
 º      John 1 1:25, Jesus said, "I am the resurrection and the life, he who  º
 º  believes in me will live, even though he dies, and he who lives and       º
 º  believes in me will never die."                                           º
 º                                                                            º
 º      Beloved husband of Roxann (Corston) Zoepel of Sudbury.  Loving        º
 º  father of "His Jewels," Madison and Zachariah.  Loving son of Carole      º
 º  (predeceased) (Husband Gilles Lefebvre) and Manfred Zoepel.  Dear         º
 º  grandson of Alice Koski of North Bay and Therese Lefebvre of              º
 º  Kapuskasing.  Dear brother of Linda (Husband John Aho), Sharon and Eric   º
 º  all of Sudbury, Laura (Husband Ron Nyssen) of lively, April (Fiancee      º
 º  Alian Claveau) of Timmins and Gil of Thunder Bay.  Sadly Missed by many   º
 º  nieces, nephews, aunts, uncles, cousins, his "Brothers", "Sisters" and    º
 º  fellow "Musketeers" resting at the Jackson and Barnard Funeral Home 233   º
 º  Larch St. Sudbury, Monday June 3rd 1996 at 11:30 am Cremation in the      º
 º  Park Lawn Crematorium.  Donations to the Madison and Zachariah Trust      º
 º  Fund would be appreciated in lieu of flowers (Friends may call 7-9 pm     º
 º  Saturday, 6-9 pm Sunday or after 11 am Monday).                           º
 º                                                                            º
 º  *PS* If you're a religious person, please say a prayer for Markus...      º
 º                                                                            º
 º       "I'll Miss ya bro.. :("                                              º

 º      Until further notice, I will be taking a vacation from the scene and  º
 º  will not be readily available to help out on Park Central.  In my         º
 º  opinion, at this point, there just isn't much that's fun about being in   º
 º  the scene and this is the main reason I will be exiting from it           º
 º  indefinitely.                                                             º
 º                                                                            º
 º      If anybody needs to contact me for any reason you can do so via       º
 º  email.  Those who know me should know my email address.                   º
 º                                                                            º

 º                                                                            º
 ÇÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄ¶
 º                                                                            º
 º      From the above, one can conclude that Crackpot has left the scene.    º
 º  He was a leader of the courier group RiSC (Rise in Superior Couriering)   º
 º  and the games group DNX (Dynamix).  It seems that he lost faith in his    º
 º  games group DNX when nearly all of DNX's members left DNX to join a       º
 º  rival group known as PSG (Prestige).                                      º
 º                                                                            º
 º      Crackpot also lost faith in his BBS, Park Central.  I only say so     º
 º  because he was always complaining to me about how Park Central was        º
 º  slowing down.  One can deduce that other BBSes were speeding up as Park   º
 º  Central was slowing down, and perhaps that scared the shit out of         º
 º  Crackpot.  Perhaps he could not deal with how his status in the scene     º
 º  was changing so fast.  The very thought that Park Central might no        º
 º  longer be #1 in the scene definitely shook him a bit.  We will never      º
 º  really know why Crackpot chose to leave the scene, but I know this, he    º
 º  will be back.. he's one of us...                                          º

 ÉÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍ»
 º                                                                            º
 º    Author  : Kilmer                                                        º
 º    Subject : In Defense of DCC                                             º
 º                                                                            º
 ÈÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍ¼
 ÉÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍ»
 º                                                                            º
 º      There is this notion within many quarters of the scene, that DCC      º
 º  couriering is not "real" couriering; that only the FTP/BBS world consist  º
 º  of the "true" couriers.  This concept is bolstered by the fact of a good  º
 º  number of generic start-up offer channels and the like.  But to toss out  º
 º  the whole area of xDCC, because a few people trade lame is extremely      º
 º  far-reaching.  And those who say "DCC is lame" are often hypocritial, as  º
 º  numerous times, for fast distro, a new release is loaded as a pack and    º
 º  sent to the FTP/BBS people in the channel.  Is DCC trading lame then?  I  º
 º  think not.                                                                º
 º                                                                            º
 º      One of the biggest complaints against DCC'ing is that the couriers    º
 º  can become "lazy" - i.e. loading a 5 pack and offering it for 3 weeks or  º
 º  something.  But DCC couriering does not exist within a vacuum.  In order  º
 º  for a real functional offer channel to survive, there needs to be some    º
 º  sort of institutional backing.  The "do-it-for-kicks" style, coupled      º
 º  with chit-chat, just doesn't cut it anymore because human nature tends    º
 º  to wind that down.  As a result, in order to have a lasting offer         º
 º  channel, one needs a "full-force" DCC team.                               º
 º                                                                            º
 º      The various procsses that a DCC'er has to go through to load a        º
 º  simple 10 pack are rather extensive.  For example, sniffing out new runs  º
 º  in various channels or grabbing the 0 day stuff from the FTPs,            º
 º  downloading it, patching different releases from various sites,           º
 º  re-zipping it in a manageable form, tagging, and then loading it va one   º
 º  of the irc scripts is hard work.  And usually one offer bot/IRC process   º
 º  is not enough.. and they must repeat it again the very next day.  And to  º
 º  then be told that "DCC"ing is lame", that would make anyone's blood       º
 º  boil.                                                                     º
 º                                                                            º
 º      And how does one really define couriering?  Is couriering simply the  º
 º  fact of moving various files from one site or board to another?  Or can   º
 º  one define couriering as the distribution of warez to the widest amount   º
 º  of people?  What exactly is the gauge?  Given this formula, the trader's  º
 º  DCC statistics during good release week can run a gig or more a day.. a   º
 º  sum total for the week, as defined by the widest amount of people, can    º
 º  easily rival any FTP upload statistics.  But these numbers are static,    º
 º  and therefore one cannot easily quantify the "DCC spread", but            º
 º  nonetheless, it is a major thrust, as evidenced by the popularity of the  º
 º  major offer channels.                                                     º
 º                                                                            º
 º      The scene should not look on DCC or any other avenue as somehow       º
 º  "less in value".  As a FTPer, I never yakked abou the BBS guys, when the  º
 º  switch was turned on to the Internet, the fast ether of the FTP world     º
 º  seemingly made trading by BBS "lame", but such is not the case, for as    º
 º  we all know, the boards still have that certain element that a FTP        º
 º  cannot give you.  And I don't care if a BBS gets telnet or not, it's      º
 º  still a viable function; even 1 to 3 node local boards have their place.  º
 º  And using the same logic, DCC's have that certain element that FTP's      º
 º  cannot give you.                                                          º
 º                                                                            º
 º      XDCC'ing is but one avenue of trading.  The BBSes are for a gauge     º
 º  guide on dupe checks and release runs; the FTP sites are for fast         º
 º  sends/gets and the DCC's are for widespread distribution.  Each has its   º
 º  place, and each has its function.                                         º
 º                                                                            º
 º                                                                            º
 ÈÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍ¼

 º                                                                            º
 º    Author  : Thastuff                                                      º
 º    Subject : Univers, Get it Straight..                                    º
 º                                                                            º
 ÈÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍ¼
 ÉÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍ»
 º                                                                            º
 º      I am writing this shortly after I read the interview that was done    º
 º  with Univers.  In that interview there were accusations made concerning   º
 º  Skyscraper, Demon, and mostly me.  I would like to explain why we did     º
 º  such a drastic thing to Univers, defend myself, and the other two, as     º
 º  well as explain the merger with AOF (Arsenists on Fire) and COPS          º
 º  (Couriers of Proven Software).                                            º
 º                                                                            º
 º      When I first came to AOF, I was as a coordinator between them and     º
 º  fATE.  I was the one who got them hooked up with having fATE as their     º
 º  official couriers.  At that time, AOF was in a really bad slump, but I    º
 º  knew that if they had the backing of a courier group, that would insure   º
 º  that AOF would be noticed and ulitmately survive.                         º
 º                                                                            º
 º      I was only a senior with AOF, but as time progressed I was doing a    º
 º  lot of the work that other seniors, and vp's (yes it was so disorganised  º
 º  that AOF had multiple vp's).  Univers noticed that and gave me a          º
 º  promotion to being a vp.  No, I did not go on some power trip, I never    º
 º  once controlled the group, I was just doing all the administrative work.  º
 º  Meanwhile, Univers would stop by now and then, I guess just to boost his  º
 º  ego.                                                                      º
 º                                                                            º
 º      During that time (I am not taking all the credit, the group had       º
 º  GREAT members, but they just needed a good leader) the group had become   º
 º  more skilled and was on it's way to become a contender with the other     º
 º  larger groups.  This is where I would like to explain Univ's statement    º
 º  about DOD duping us.  DOD did not dupe us, but we were accused of duping  º
 º  them (Borland C++ v5.0 Febuary Beta).  But shortly after, the suppliers   º
 º  went into a slump, and the leader did not his job.                        º
 º                                                                            º
 º      After consulting with Skyscraper, we decided (as two                  º
 º  vice-presidents), that we needed full control of the group to make it     º
 º  survive.  We had planned it for a couple weeks before it actually         º
 º  happened, and during that time Demon was brought into it for additional   º
 º  senior support.  Basically the seniors who did work, wanted to get rid    º
 º  of those who didn't.                                                      º
 º                                                                            º
 º      Then came the magic day.  We had a program to release, but shortly    º
 º  before I was done packaging it, some no-name group released it.           º
 º  Obviously I stopped packaging it as there was no use releasing a dupe,    º
 º  and told Univers I stopped packaging it.  He told me to keep packaging,   º
 º  and I told him it would be a dupe (He knew that someone already released  º
 º  it).  I simply stated that "I refuse to release it", and that's when he   º
 º  said "You're fired!".                                                     º
 º                                                                            º
 º      Before I lost my place in the group I knew that the takeover had to   º
 º  be done right then and there.  It was about an hour after the arguments   º
 º  that Univers said, and I quote "thastuff, you can have AOF...  AND SHOVE  º
 º  IT UP YOU ASS!", he left, and I think immediatly joined MTY as a senior   º
 º  or something.                                                             º
 º                                                                            º
 º      Skyscrape, Demon, and I became the leaders of AOF, there weren't any  º
 º  other vp's or seniors, and this made AOF much more politics free, and     º
 º  easier to manage.  We made more releases, and for a couple weeks were     º
 º  quite content.  But then real life stepped in, no matter how bad timing   º
 º  it was, forced me to leave the scene for nearly a month.  I had less      º
 º  then a week to do something with AOF so it didn't just die as a result    º
 º  of all my actions.                                                        º
 º                                                                            º
 º      I had been approched by Endeavour (For the record, I have always      º
 º  felt COPS was lame), to merge with COPS.  This was the best thing I       º
 º  could do for the remaining AOF members.  I made the merge happen, got     º
 º  all the AOF members a spot in COPS, and felt satisfied that I didn't do   º
 º  the selfish thing and just leave.  That is when I resigned from COPS as   º
 º  a senior, and dealt with life.                                            º
 º                                                                            º
 º      Now that this is all over, I would like to ask everyone who reads     º
 º  interviews and articles that they are completely onesided.  Please don't  º
 º  believe the first thing you read, but listen to both sides, and judge     º
 º  for yourself what is right.  Everyone that knows me knows that I am far   º
 º  from having an ego, and I have no need to go on power trips as Univers    º
 º  described for you.  I don't want any wars with Univers, as it would be a  º
 º  complete waste of time since he has no real place in the scene.  I got    º
 º  him his place in the scene, and yes, with power, I took it away.          º
 º                                                                            º
 º                                                                            º
 ÈÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍ¼

 º                                                                            º
 º    Author  : Tuxedo Mask                                                   º
 º    Subject : Windows 95                                                    º
 º                                                                            º
 ÈÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍ¼
