 º                                                                            º
 º      The major hurdle to gaming on the PC has always been ease of use.     º
 º  Installing DOS games has traditionally been even more difficult than      º
 º  installing other PC software.  With multiple standards for video cards,   º
 º  memory hassles created by DOS' 640kb basic memory limit, and the general  º
 º  user-unfriendliness of the system, getting games to actually work is      º
 º  sometimes more of a challenge than the games themselves.  Some DOS games  º
 º  suffer a 35% or greater return rate to software stores simply because     º
 º  they cannot be successfully installed on the user's hardware.             º
 º                                                                            º
 º      Developing games for a DOS-based PC results in similar nightmares,    º
 º  as game programmers have to write routines for every single video card,   º
 º  sound card, and possible system set-up in advance.  It's no surprise      º
 º  that they often failed to cover all possible combinations.  And it's      º
 º  similarly unsurprising that this has generally left PC games the strict   º
 º  domain of hard-core gamers and computer enthusiasts.                      º
 º                                                                            º
 º      With Windows 95, Microsoft seeks to change all this.  Not only does   º
 º  Windows 95 make installation easier, it also makes game development       º
 º  easier, thanks to a series of developer APIs (Application Programming     º
 º  Interface) and libraries known as the Game SDK (Software Development      º
 º  Kit).  To get the Game SDK, developers must simply join the Microsoft     º
 º  Developer's Network, which costs around $500 per year - about the cost    º
 º  of goods of the CDs and manuals the average developer receives in that    º
 º  time.  Microsoft then supplies these software libraries to game           º
 º  developers, making the process of developing a game designed to wirk      º
 º  within Windows 95 a whole lot easier.  The major component of the SDK is  º
 º  the series of APIs known as DirectX.                                      º
 º                                                                            º
 º      The main complaint about developing for Windows is that, as a         º
 º  program that puts a layer of software between the hardware and the user,  º
 º  it simply cannot provde the performance needed for a high-speed game.     º
 º  To get a game to run faster under Windows, developers generally have to   º
 º  break all sorts of rules - resulting in the same basic headaches that     º
 º  occur under DOS.  DirectX, by providing a set of standard APIs, fixes     º
 º  some of this.  Microsoft has "broken the rules" of standard Windows       º
 º  development to gain speed (such as DirectDraw's ability to write          º
 º  straight to VRAM in a window).  And as long as developers stick to the    º
 º  "broken rules" Microsoft has developed for the DirectX APIs (written in   º
 º  extremely low-level code), everything will run fine.  The advance of      º
 º  Moore's Law (which, pared down, says that hardware keeps getting faster   º
 º  and cheaper) also has helped lessen complaints about performance under    º
 º  Windows.                                                                  º
 º                                                                            º
 º      By writing to the DirectX specifications, developers can be sure      º
 º  that their software will run on any PC running Windows 95.  Microsoft     º
 º  takes care of the irritating task of developing drivers for all the       º
 º  different types of hardware that the game might be played on, not to      º
 º  mention doing extensive compatibility testing.  The time and effort       º
 º  saved by being able to write to one spec also decreases development time  º
 º  and cost.                                                                 º
 º                                                                            º
 º      More importantly than just making it easier to develop and play       º
 º  games on a PC, the Direct X APIs make practical for the first time        º
 º  something that has always been possible on PCs - Plugn 'n' Play, or       º
 º  widespread support for a variety of novel hardware.  This is the          º
 º  single-most exciting aspect of Windows 95 as a gaming platform, and it    º
 º  is not an understatement to say that this could be the single-most        º
 º  important advance in PC gaming technology in the last decade.             º
 º                                                                            º
 º      Until now, if a hardware developer created or implemented a new       º
 º  technology, like 2D or 3D graphics acceleration, a new input device, a    º
 º  new sound card, or anything that took the PC past the stock "vanilla"     º
 º  stage, they would find that they had created an orphan technology, at     º
 º  least as far as game developers are concerned.  Until the device gained   º
 º  enough acceptance in the marketplace (until it sold enough units), few    º
 º  companies would go through the trouble of writing the drivers to support  º
 º  it.  Without the games, few upgrades would be sold, and few new           º
 º  technologies were adopted.  For example, despite the fact that            º
 º  practically every graphics card sold since the introduction of the 486    º
 º  has had 2D graphics acceleration, few PC games have ever taken advantage  º
 º  of it.                                                                    º
 º                                                                            º
 º      The only real advantage to emerge on the PC since the days of         º
 º  Creative Labs' Sound Blaster card was the pathetic MPC (Multimedia PC),   º
 º  a Windows-based standard developed at the dawn of the multimedia age.     º
 º  With an MPC compliant PC, all you could really be sure of was that your   º
 º  machine could run the latest and greatest encyclopedia CD-ROM, but        º
 º  that's about it.  Snore.  Now that's all different.  With Microsoft       º
 º  developing (or more correctly, having hardware manufacturers develop)     º
 º  drivers for every hardware device conceivable, developers can now         º
 º  blithely write to the spec and not worry about supporting various         º
 º  hardware elements.  If additional hardware is there, DirectX will sense   º
 º  and use it.  If not, the CPU will emulate the missing hardware, when      º
 º  possible.  If you have no sound card, there's not much the DirectSound    º
 º  is goiong to be able to do with a stock PC speaker.                       º
 º                                                                            º
 º      Not every developer, however, is totally thrilled with the Game SDK.  º
 º  It's also important to note that because DirectX's features are present   º
 º  in software, fairly powerful machines are needed to be able to take       º
 º  advantage of DirectX in any practical way.  It's clear that with the      º
 º  introduction and continued support of the DirectX APIs (which were        º
 º  developed with strong input from leading PC game companies), Microsoft    º
 º  is making an intense effort to support Windows 95 as a game platform.     º
 º  In the short term, the reason why is equally clear.  Despite what people  º
 º  say to themselves to justify the purchase of an expensive home PC, games  º
 º  are the most popular home application, by far.  To ensure that Windows    º
 º  95 is accepted as an OS in the home, then, there must be a game presence  º
 º  in it.  Especially considering that first-tiem buyers of home PCs are     º
 º  far less likely to withstand rigors of installing a DOS game.  As this    º
 º  all passes, the PC market is guaranteed to see more game titles released  º
 º  native to Windows 95, and as a result, more games released by the top     º
 º  games groups will also be native to Windows 95.                           º
 º                                                                            º
 º                                                                            º
 ÈÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍ¼

 ÉÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍ»
 º                                                                            º

 º    Subject : Group Reviews : Games                                         º
 º                                                                            º
 ÈÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍ¼

 ÉÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍ»
 º                                                                            º
 º      Hello, and welcome to Reality Check Network's all new group review!   º
 º  Here I will be reviewing the 5 best games release groups in the scene.    º
 º  Well, actually, *I* won't be the one reviewing them, *THEY* will be!      º
 º  It's all up to the groups, this is where quantity DOES count, but you     º
 º  will soon enough find that quality by far outweighs quantity.  Let's      º
 º  review the criteria I'll be using for judging releases.  The following    º
 º  is the scoring basis I'll be using :                                      º
 º                                                                            º
 º  Points :                                                                  º
 º  --------                                                                  º
 º                                                                            º
 º  [-3] The game didn't work and a crack/fix was not released within 72      º
 º       hours.  The group may regain the 3 lost points by releasing a crack  º
 º       or fix, even beyond the 3 day period.                                º
 º                                                                            º
 º  [ 1] The game was a dupe or freeware,                                     º
 º                                                                            º
 º  [ 2] Unsatisfactory,                                                      º
 º                                                                            º
 º  [ 3] Average,                                                             º
 º                                                                            º
 º  [ 4] Above Average, and                                                   º
 º                                                                            º
 º  [ 5] Excellent!                                                           º
 º                                                                            º
 º      A group may lose points the following week and have their releases    º
 º  labeled as broken (thus receiving the proper amout of points).  If the    º
 º  group has released a fix between the two issues, we'll give them credit   º
 º  accordingly.  If a group releases a fix within a 3 day period, the        º
 º  game will be rated as if it worked in the first place, thus getting the   º
 º  3 points it lost back and any points it would have earned.  If a group    º
 º  releases a fix after the 3 day period has expired, it will receive its 3  º
 º  points back, but get no more.  Betas may receive no more than 3 points.   º
 º                                                                            º
 ÌÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍ¹

 ÉÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍ»
 º                                                                            º
 º      Hello, and welcome to Reality Check Network's all new group review!   º
 º  Here I will be reviewing the 5 best games release groups in the scene.    º
 º  Well, actually, *I* won't be the one reviewing them, *THEY* will be!      º
 º  It's all up to the groups, this is where quantity DOES count, but you     º
 º  will soon enough find that quality by far outweighs quantity.  Let's      º
 º  review the criteria I'll be using for judging releases.  The following    º
 º  is the scoring basis I'll be using :                                      º
 º                                                                            º
 º  Points :                                                                  º
 º  --------                                                                  º
 º                                                                            º
 º  [-3] The game didn't work and a crack/fix was not released within 72      º
 º       hours.  The group may regain the 3 lost points by releasing a crack  º
 º       or fix, even beyond the 3 day period.                                º
 º                                                                            º
 º  [ 1] The game was a dupe or freeware,                                     º
 º                                                                            º
 º  [ 2] Unsatisfactory,                                                      º
 º                                                                            º
 º  [ 3] Average,                                                             º
 º                                                                            º
 º  [ 4] Above Average, and                                                   º
 º                                                                            º
 º  [ 5] Excellent!                                                           º
 º                                                                            º
 º      A group may lose points the following week and have their releases    º
 º  labeled as broken (thus receiving the proper amout of points).  If the    º
 º  group has released a fix between the two issues, we'll give them credit   º
 º  accordingly.  If a group releases a fix within a 3 day period, the        º
 º  game will be rated as if it worked in the first place, thus getting the   º
 º  3 points it lost back and any points it would have earned.  If a group    º
 º  releases a fix after the 3 day period has expired, it will receive its 3  º
 º  points back, but get no more.  Betas may receive no more than 3 points.   º
 º                                                                            º
 ÌÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍ¹

 º                                                                            º
 º      Hello, and welcome to Reality Check Network's all new group review!   º
 º  Here I will be reviewing the 5 best games release groups in the scene.    º
 º  Well, actually, *I* won't be the one reviewing them, *THEY* will be!      º
 º  It's all up to the groups, this is where quantity DOES count, but you     º
 º  will soon enough find that quality by far outweighs quantity.  Let's      º
 º  review the criteria I'll be using for judging releases.  The following    º
 º  is the scoring basis I'll be using :                                      º
 º                                                                            º
 º  Points :                                                                  º
 º  --------                                                                  º
 º                                                                            º
 º  [-3] The game didn't work and a crack/fix was not released within 72      º
 º       hours.  The group may regain the 3 lost points by releasing a crack  º
 º       or fix, even beyond the 3 day period.                                º
 º                                                                            º
 º  [ 1] The game was a dupe or freeware,                                     º
 º                                                                            º
 º  [ 2] Unsatisfactory,                                                      º
 º                                                                            º
 º  [ 3] Average,                                                             º
 º                                                                            º
 º  [ 4] Above Average, and                                                   º
 º                                                                            º
 º  [ 5] Excellent!                                                           º
 º                                                                            º
 º      A group may lose points the following week and have their releases    º
 º  labeled as broken (thus receiving the proper amout of points).  If the    º
 º  group has released a fix between the two issues, we'll give them credit   º
 º  accordingly.  If a group releases a fix within a 3 day period, the        º
 º  game will be rated as if it worked in the first place, thus getting the   º
 º  3 points it lost back and any points it would have earned.  If a group    º
 º  releases a fix after the 3 day period has expired, it will receive its 3  º
 º  points back, but get no more.  Betas may receive no more than 3 points.   º
 º                                                                            º

 ÉÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍ»
 º                                                                            º
 º      Hello, and welcome to Reality Check Network's all new group review!   º
 º  Here I will be reviewing the 5 best games release groups in the scene.    º
 º  Well, actually, *I* won't be the one reviewing them, *THEY* will be!      º
 º  It's all up to the groups, this is where quantity DOES count, but you     º
 º  will soon enough find that quality by far outweighs quantity.  Let's      º
 º  review the criteria I'll be using for judging releases.  The following    º
 º  is the scoring basis I'll be using :                                      º
 º                                                                            º
 º  Points :                                                                  º
 º  --------                                                                  º
 º                                                                            º
 º  [-3] The game didn't work and a crack/fix was not released within 72      º
 º       hours.  The group may regain the 3 lost points by releasing a crack  º
 º       or fix, even beyond the 3 day period.                                º
 º                                                                            º
 º  [ 1] The game was a dupe or freeware,                                     º
 º                                                                            º
 º  [ 2] Unsatisfactory,                                                      º
 º                                                                            º
 º  [ 3] Average,                                                             º
 º                                                                            º
 º  [ 4] Above Average, and                                                   º
 º                                                                            º
 º  [ 5] Excellent!                                                           º
 º                                                                            º
 º      A group may lose points the following week and have their releases    º
 º  labeled as broken (thus receiving the proper amout of points).  If the    º
 º  group has released a fix between the two issues, we'll give them credit   º
 º  accordingly.  If a group releases a fix within a 3 day period, the        º
 º  game will be rated as if it worked in the first place, thus getting the   º
 º  3 points it lost back and any points it would have earned.  If a group    º
 º  releases a fix after the 3 day period has expired, it will receive its 3  º
 º  points back, but get no more.  Betas may receive no more than 3 points.   º
 º                                                                            º

 ÉÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍ»
 º                                                                            º
 º      Hello, and welcome to Reality Check Network's all new group review!   º
 º  Here I will be reviewing the 5 best utils release groups in the scene.    º
 º  Well, actually, *I* won't be the one reviewing them, *THEY* will be!      º
 º  It's all up to the groups, this is where quantity DOES count, but you     º
 º  will soon enough find that quality by far outweighs quantity.  Let's      º
 º  review the criteria I'll be using for judging releases.  The following    º
 º  is the scoring basis I'll be using :                                      º
 º                                                                            º
 º  Points :                                                                  º
 º  --------                                                                  º
 º                                                                            º
 º  [-3] The util didn't work and a crack/fix was not released within 72      º
 º       hours.  The group may regain the 3 lost points by releasing a crack  º
 º       or fix, even beyond the 3 day period.                                º
 º                                                                            º
 º  [ 1] The util was a dupe or freeware,                                     º
 º                                                                            º
 º  [ 2] Unsatisfactory,                                                      º
 º                                                                            º
 º  [ 3] Average,                                                             º
 º                                                                            º
 º  [ 4] Above Average, and                                                   º
 º                                                                            º
 º  [ 5] Excellent!                                                           º
 º                                                                            º
 º      A group may lose points the following week and have their releases    º
 º  labeled as broken (thus receiving the proper amout of points).  If the    º
 º  group has released a fix between the two issues, we'll give them credit   º
 º  accordingly.  If a group releases a fix within a 3 day period, the        º
 º  util will be rated as if it worked in the first place, thus getting the   º
 º  3 points it lost back and any points it would have earned.  If a group    º
 º  releases a fix after the 3 day period has expired, it will receive its 3  º
 º  points back, but get no more.  Betas may receive no more than 3 points.   º
 º                                                                            º
 ÌÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍ¹

 ÉÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍ»
 º                                                                            º
 º      Hello, and welcome to Reality Check Network's all new group review!   º
 º  Here I will be reviewing the 5 best utils release groups in the scene.    º
 º  Well, actually, *I* won't be the one reviewing them, *THEY* will be!      º
 º  It's all up to the groups, this is where quantity DOES count, but you     º
 º  will soon enough find that quality by far outweighs quantity.  Let's      º
 º  review the criteria I'll be using for judging releases.  The following    º
 º  is the scoring basis I'll be using :                                      º
 º                                                                            º
 º  Points :                                                                  º
 º  --------                                                                  º
 º                                                                            º
 º  [-3] The util didn't work and a crack/fix was not released within 72      º
 º       hours.  The group may regain the 3 lost points by releasing a crack  º
 º       or fix, even beyond the 3 day period.                                º
 º                                                                            º
 º  [ 1] The util was a dupe or freeware,                                     º
 º                                                                            º
 º  [ 2] Unsatisfactory,                                                      º
 º                                                                            º
 º  [ 3] Average,                                                             º
 º                                                                            º
 º  [ 4] Above Average, and                                                   º
 º                                                                            º
 º  [ 5] Excellent!                                                           º
 º                                                                            º
 º      A group may lose points the following week and have their releases    º
 º  labeled as broken (thus receiving the proper amout of points).  If the    º
 º  group has released a fix between the two issues, we'll give them credit   º
 º  accordingly.  If a group releases a fix within a 3 day period, the        º
 º  util will be rated as if it worked in the first place, thus getting the   º
 º  3 points it lost back and any points it would have earned.  If a group    º
 º  releases a fix after the 3 day period has expired, it will receive its 3  º
 º  points back, but get no more.  Betas may receive no more than 3 points.   º
 º                                                                            º

 º                                                                            º
 º      Hello, and welcome to Reality Check Network's all new group review!   º
 º  Here I will be reviewing the 5 best utils release groups in the scene.    º
 º  Well, actually, *I* won't be the one reviewing them, *THEY* will be!      º
 º  It's all up to the groups, this is where quantity DOES count, but you     º
 º  will soon enough find that quality by far outweighs quantity.  Let's      º
 º  review the criteria I'll be using for judging releases.  The following    º
 º  is the scoring basis I'll be using :                                      º
 º                                                                            º
 º  Points :                                                                  º
 º  --------                                                                  º
 º                                                                            º
 º  [-3] The util didn't work and a crack/fix was not released within 72      º
 º       hours.  The group may regain the 3 lost points by releasing a crack  º
 º       or fix, even beyond the 3 day period.                                º
 º                                                                            º
 º  [ 1] The util was a dupe or freeware,                                     º
 º                                                                            º
 º  [ 2] Unsatisfactory,                                                      º
 º                                                                            º
 º  [ 3] Average,                                                             º
 º                                                                            º
 º  [ 4] Above Average, and                                                   º
 º                                                                            º
 º  [ 5] Excellent!                                                           º
 º                                                                            º
 º      A group may lose points the following week and have their releases    º
 º  labeled as broken (thus receiving the proper amout of points).  If the    º
 º  group has released a fix between the two issues, we'll give them credit   º
 º  accordingly.  If a group releases a fix within a 3 day period, the        º
 º  util will be rated as if it worked in the first place, thus getting the   º
 º  3 points it lost back and any points it would have earned.  If a group    º
 º  releases a fix after the 3 day period has expired, it will receive its 3  º
 º  points back, but get no more.  Betas may receive no more than 3 points.   º
 º                                                                            º

 º      Hello, and welcome to Reality Check Network's all new group review!   º
 º  Here I will be reviewing the 5 best utils release groups in the scene.    º
 º  Well, actually, *I* won't be the one reviewing them, *THEY* will be!      º
 º  It's all up to the groups, this is where quantity DOES count, but you     º
 º  will soon enough find that quality by far outweighs quantity.  Let's      º
 º  review the criteria I'll be using for judging releases.  The following    º
 º  is the scoring basis I'll be using :                                      º
 º                                                                            º
 º  Points :                                                                  º
 º  --------                                                                  º
 º                                                                            º
 º  [-3] The util didn't work and a crack/fix was not released within 72      º
 º       hours.  The group may regain the 3 lost points by releasing a crack  º
 º       or fix, even beyond the 3 day period.                                º
 º                                                                            º
 º  [ 1] The util was a dupe or freeware,                                     º
 º                                                                            º
 º  [ 2] Unsatisfactory,                                                      º
 º                                                                            º
 º  [ 3] Average,                                                             º
 º                                                                            º
 º  [ 4] Above Average, and                                                   º
 º                                                                            º
 º  [ 5] Excellent!                                                           º
 º                                                                            º
 º      A group may lose points the following week and have their releases    º
 º  labeled as broken (thus receiving the proper amout of points).  If the    º
 º  group has released a fix between the two issues, we'll give them credit   º
 º  accordingly.  If a group releases a fix within a 3 day period, the        º
 º  util will be rated as if it worked in the first place, thus getting the   º
 º  3 points it lost back and any points it would have earned.  If a group    º
 º  releases a fix after the 3 day period has expired, it will receive its 3  º
 º  points back, but get no more.  Betas may receive no more than 3 points.   º

 ÉÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍ»

 º  Dear Road Rebel,                                                          º
 º                                                                            º
 º      The BBS scene pimped on the Internet scene.  It was so much more      º
 º  interesting to be in!  I mean getting stuff around in 0-2 day was HARD!   º
 º  It took skilled couriers.  I think the Internet ruined everything.        º
 º                                                                            º
 º                                               Signed,                      º
 º                                                  Koon Dog                  º
 º                                                                            º
 ÇÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄ¶
 º                                                                            º
 º  Dear Koon Dog,                                                            º
 º                                                                            º
 º      I think you're very right, the BBS scene involved much more skill.    º
 º  People would spend countless hours logging onto boards around the world   º
 º  to get new releases so they could put everything around the world and     º
 º  get all the releases out.  But why do you think the Internet ruined       º
 º  EVERYTHING?  I think it raised the competition that much higher.  Now     º
 º  people really have to try hard to get places before others do.  When the  º
 º  Internet wasn't around, the competition was not to get stuff around       º
 º  faster than anybody else, but to get stuff around at all.  Now, we have   º
 º  so many great couriers and they all try to push the same stuff to the     º
 º  same place, and people lose by mere seconds.  I think that makes things   º
 º  that much harder.  But of course, "it is not who does it first, it's who  º
 º  does it right," and it could quite easily be said that much of today's    º
 º  scene is filled with bad releases that don't work.                        º
 º                                                                            º
 º                                               Signed,                      º
 º                                                  Road Rebel                º
 º                                                                            º
 ÌÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍ¹
 º                                                                            º
 º  Dear Road Rebel,                                                          º
 º                                                                            º
 º          The Internet has fixed some things and fucked up other things.    º
 º  Couriers are having a ball now trying to do things before others.         º
 º  However, like you say, there are some new problems.  Many boards are      º
 º  getting partial releases and that doesn't help anybody.  It makes the     º
 º  courier look bad and then makes the group look stupid.  Ultimately, it    º
 º  lowers the quality of the board.                                          º
 º                                                                            º
 º                                               Signed,                      º
 º                                                  Zero Prime                º
 º                                                                            º
 ÇÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄÄ¶
 º                                                                            º
 º  Dear Reader,                                                              º
 º                                                                            º
 º      I think you bring out an interesting point.  The scene is currently   º
 º  in a transition regarding the Internet and the BBS scene.  The Internet,  º
 º  I think, will end up prevailing, but while we're making this transition   º
 º  from BBS to Internet, the two are clashing.  We're going from one         º
 º  resource that can push a meg per second, to a resource that pushes no     º
 º  more than 3k per second.  That's a huge bottleneck, and one that will be  º
 º  resolved as soon as we start getting BBSs running on private T1's and     º
 º  Cable modems.  Until then, the bottleneck will still slow us down.  As    º
 º  soon as the transition is complete, the scene will breathe a fresher      º
 º  air.                                                                      º
 º                                                                            º
 º                                               Signed,                      º
 º                                                  Road Rebel                º
 º                                                                            º
 ÌÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍÍ¹
 º                                                                            º
 º  Topic For Next Week : Week Old Group                                      º
 º                                                                            º
 º          As always, we see about three new groups a week, and about three  º
 º  more die every week.  However, none of these groups grow beyond 2 or 3    º
 º  releases.  Every once in a while, if we're lucky, the group ends up       º
 º  releasing on a regular basis.  Sounds like a winner, right?  Wrong.       º
 º  Most often, the group's releases don't work, are uncracked, or even       º
 º  incomplete.  One would think, in theory, that new groups can't hurt       º
 º  anything.  Sure, there could be too many of them, and they take up time,  º
 º  but if they release, they're helping the scene.  However, this is hardly  º
 º  the case.                                                                 º
 º                                                                            º
 º      The situation has become so bad that now, when one finds a release    º
 º  that he wants, he must check twice to see what group released it.         º
 º  Often, if the group is not a megafigure such as DOD or PWA, Razor or      º
 º  Dynamix, he won't even download it, for fear of wasting an hour of his    º
 º  time just to find that what he downloaded doesn't even work.  So, what's  º
 º  the alternative for the hopefuls to get big in the scene?  What do you    º
 º  think these small groups are doing to the scene as a whole?  Do you       º
 º  think they benefit it, or inhibit its success?  Do you think their        º
 º  releases, even though small in number, are worth downloading?  Do you     º
 º  trust them?  Write back and tell us what you think!                       º
 º                                                                            º
